# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM Pass Manager Registration and Execution Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a new LLVM optimization pass is registered and executed in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files that define: the PassManager template, the PassRegistry, the pass add() registration, and the pass execution order in the standard optimization pipeline (O2/O3).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

There\n11: /// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n18: /// single module provided.\n19: ///\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\n21: /// modules and functions.\n22: ///\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\n24: ///   a Function.\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\n26: ///\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \"Value Semantics and Concept-based\n29: /// Polymorphism\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \"Inheritance Is The Base\n30: /// Class of Evil\") by Sean Parent:\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\n32: /// * http://www.yout

67-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive analysis of the LLVM pass manager registration and execution chain. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**PassManager Template** (`llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h`):
- Generic template `PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>` that manages sequential pass execution
- `addPass()` method wraps heterogeneous passes using the PassModel concept wrapper
- `run()` method executes all passes sequentially with analysis manager support
- `ModulePassManager` is a typedef specialization for Module-level passes

**PassRegistry System**:
- Global singleton registry (`llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h`) maintaining PassInfo metadata
- `PassInfo` stores pass name, command-line argument, type ID, and constructor
- `registerPass()` maintains two maps: one for type-based lookup, one for string-based lookup
- Registration macros (`INITIALIZE_PASS`, `RegisterPass<T>`) simplify pass registration

**Concept-Based Polymorphism** (`llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h`):
- `PassConcept` defines the abstract interface for all passes
- `PassModel<PassT>` wraps individual pass implementations, enabling storage of heterogeneous types in a single vector

**Pipeline Construction** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp`):
- `buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline()` is the entry point (O0-O3)
- `buildModuleSimplificationPipeline()` adds early canonicalization passes
- `buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()` adds late-stage optimization passes
- O3-specific passes: `CallSiteSplittingPass` (line 1152) and `ControlHeightReductionPass` (line 1566)

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file references, symbol definitions, and a detailed narrative explanation of the entire system.

It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\\n164: public:\\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\\n167: \\n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\\n171:   // duplicated code here.\\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\\n173: \\n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\\n176:     return *this;\\n177:   }\\n178: \\n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\\\",\\\");\\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\\n183:       OS << LS;\\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\\n185:     }\\n186:   }\\n187: \\n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\\n202:   }\\n203: \\n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\\n209:   template <typename PassT>\\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\\n214:   }\\n215: \\n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\\n218: \\n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\\n220: \\n221: protected:\\n222:   using PassConceptT =\\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n224: \\n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\\n226: };\\n227: \\n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\\n230: \\n231: template <>\\n232: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n233:                                                    const Module &IR);\\n234: \\n235: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Module>;\\n236: \\n237: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over modules.\\n238: using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;\\n239: \\n240: template <>\\n241: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n242:                                                      const Function &IR);\\n243: \\n244: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Function>;\\n245: \\n246: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over functions.\\n247: using FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>;\\n248: \\n249: /// A container for analyses that lazily runs them and caches their\\n250: /// results.\\n251: ///\\n252: /// This class can manage analyses for any IR unit where the address of the IR\\n253: /// unit sufficies as its identity.\\n254: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... template-based architecture defined in llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h. The PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...> template (lines 159-226) implements a generic pass manager that can manage passes over any IR unit (Module, Function, Loop, etc.). This template provides:\\n\\n1. **addPass() method** (lines 193-214): Accepts a pass instance and wraps it in a PassModel concept wrapper, storing it in a std::vector for sequential execution\\n2. **run() method** (lines 190-191): Executes all contained passes sequentially over the IR unit, propagating the AnalysisManager to each pass for dependency resolution\\n3. **PreservedAnalyses tracking**: Each pass reports which analyses it preserves, enabling the AnalysisManager to invalidate stale results\\n\\nThe ModulePassManager typedef (line 238) is a convenience specialization for Module-level passes: `using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;`\\n\\n## PassRegistry Registration System\\n\\nPass registration follows a two-tier system defined in llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h and implemented in llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp:\\n\\n1. **PassInfo metadata** (llvm/include/llvm/PassInfo.h, lines 29-89): Each pass has a PassInfo instance containing:\\n   - PassName: Display name of the pass\\n   - PassArgument: Command-line argument to invoke the pass\\n   - PassID: Type-erased identifier (&MyPass::ID)\\n   - NormalCtor: Default constructor function pointer\\n\\n2. **PassRegistry::registerPass()** (llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp, lines 48-62): Global singleton registry that maintains two maps:\\n   - PassInfoMap: Maps PassID (void*) to PassInfo pointer\\n   - PassInfoStringMap: Maps PassArgument (StringRef) to PassInfo pointer\\n   - Listeners: PassRegistrationListener callbacks for observers\\n\\n3. **Registration macros** (llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h, lines 39-58):\\n   - INITIALIZE_PASS_BEGIN/END: Defines a pass initialization function that creates PassInfo and registers it\\n   - RegisterPass<T> template (lines 89-98): Simple registration helper that calls PassRegistry::registerPass()\\n\\n## Pass Concept and Polymorphism\\n\\nThe pass system uses concept-based polymorphism (not inheritance) defined in llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h:\\n\\n1. **PassConcept** (lines 40-63): Abstract interface for pass objects with virtual methods:\\n   - run(IRUnitT&, AnalysisManagerT&, ExtraArgTs...): Executes the pass\\n   - printPipeline(): Prints pass name for debugging\\n   - isRequired(): Indicates if pass should skip instrumentation\\n\\n2. **PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>** (lines 72-114): Type-erased wrapper that adapts any pass object conforming to the run() protocol into the PassConcept interface. This enables storing heterogeneous pass types in a single vector.\\n\\n## Pipeline Construction: PassBuilder\\n\\nThe PassBuilder class (llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h) orchestrates standard optimization pipelines:\\n\\n1. **buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline()** (llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp, lines 1715-1761):\\n   - Entry point for O0-O3 pipeline construction\\n   - Calls buildModuleSimplificationPipeline(Level, Phase) at line 1746\\n   - Calls buildModuleOptimizationPipeline(Level, Phase) at line 1749\\n   - Returns a ModulePassManager containing the complete pipeline\\n\\n2. **buildModuleSimplificationPipeline()** (lines 1091-1474):\\n   - Adds early canonicalization and cleanup passes\\n   - O3-specific: CallSiteSplittingPass at line 1152 (only for O3)\\n   - Includes: ForceFunctionAttrsPass, InferFunctionAttrsPass, IPSCCPPass, GlobalOptPass, etc.\\n\\n3. **buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()** (lines 1478-1700):\\n   - Adds late-stage optimization passes after inlining\\n   - O3-specific: ControlHeightReductionPass at line 1566 (EnableCHR && Level == OptimizationLevel::O3)\\n   - Includes: PartialInlinerPass, loop optimizations, vectorization (addVectorPasses), LoopSinkPass\\n\\n## Execution Order in O2/O3 Pipeline\\n\\nThe standard optimization pipeline for O2 and O3 follows this order:\\n\\n1. **Module Simplification Phase**:\\n   - Annotation2MetadataPass\\n   - ForceFunctionAttrsPass\\n   - InferFunctionAttrsPass, CoroEarlyPass\\n   - Function-level simplification (EarlyCSE, SROA, SimplifyCFG)\\n   - CallSiteSplittingPass (O3 only)\\n   - IPSCCPPass, GlobalOptPass, DeadArgumentEliminationPass\\n   - Function attribute inference (FunctionAttrsPass)\\n   - Jump threading, GVN, DSE\\n\\n2. **Module Inlining Phase**:\\n   - ModuleInlinerWrapperPass with CGSCC passes\\n   - Post-inlining simplification\\n\\n3. **Module Optimization Phase**:\\n   - PartialInlinerPass\\n   - ReversePostOrderFunctionAttrsPass\\n   - Function optimization pipeline:\\n     - Loop optimizations (LoopRotate, LoopDeletion, LoopInterchange)\\n     - Loop fusion, distribution\\n     - Vectorization (SLP, Loop vectorization)\\n     - ControlHeightReductionPass (O3 only)\\n     - LoopSinkPass\\n   - Final SimplifyCFG and instruction combining\\n\\n## Key Files Summary\\n\\n- **llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h**: Core template and ModulePassManager definition\\n- **llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h**: PassRegistry declaration\\n- **llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp**: Pass registration implementation\\n- **llvm/include/llvm/PassInfo.h**: PassInfo metadata structure\\n- **llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h**: Registration macros and RegisterPass template\\n- **llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h**: PassConcept and PassModel implementations\\n- **llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h**: PassBuilder API declaration\\n- **llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp**: Pipeline construction implementations\\n- **llvm/include/llvm/InitializePasses.h**: Pass initialization declarations\"\n}\n",
